     103             : /************************************************************************/
     104             : /*                              RasterIO()                              */
     105             : /************************************************************************/
     106             : 
     107             : /**
     108             :  * \fn GDALRasterBand::IRasterIO( GDALRWFlag eRWFlag,
     109             :  *                                int nXOff, int nYOff, int nXSize, int nYSize,
     110             :  *                                void * pData, int nBufXSize, int nBufYSize,
     111             :  *                                GDALDataType eBufType,
     112             :  *                                GSpacing nPixelSpace,
     113             :  *                                GSpacing nLineSpace,
     114             :  *                                GDALRasterIOExtraArg* psExtraArg )
     115             :  * \brief Read/write a region of image data for this band.
     116             :  *
     117             :  * This method allows reading a region of a GDALRasterBand into a buffer,
     118             :  * or writing data from a buffer into a region of a GDALRasterBand. It
     119             :  * automatically takes care of data type translation if the data type
     120             :  * (eBufType) of the buffer is different than that of the GDALRasterBand.
     121             :  * The method also takes care of image decimation / replication if the
     122             :  * buffer size (nBufXSize x nBufYSize) is different than the size of the
     123             :  * region being accessed (nXSize x nYSize).
     124             :  *
     125             :  * The nPixelSpace and nLineSpace parameters allow reading into or
     126             :  * writing from unusually organized buffers. This is primarily used
     127             :  * for buffers containing more than one bands raster data in interleaved
     128             :  * format.
     129             :  *
     130             :  * Some formats may efficiently implement decimation into a buffer by
     131             :  * reading from lower resolution overview images.
     132             :  *
     133             :  * For highest performance full resolution data access, read and write
     134             :  * on "block boundaries" as returned by GetBlockSize(), or use the
     135             :  * ReadBlock() and WriteBlock() methods.
     136             :  *
     137             :  * This method is the same as the C GDALRasterIO() or GDALRasterIOEx() functions.
     138             :  *
     139             :  * @param eRWFlag Either GF_Read to read a region of data, or GF_Write to
     140             :  * write a region of data.
     141             :  *
     142             :  * @param nXOff The pixel offset to the top left corner of the region
     143             :  * of the band to be accessed. This would be zero to start from the left side.
     144             :  *
     145             :  * @param nYOff The line offset to the top left corner of the region
     146             :  * of the band to be accessed. This would be zero to start from the top.
     147             :  *
     148             :  * @param nXSize The width of the region of the band to be accessed in pixels.
     149             :  *
     150             :  * @param nYSize The height of the region of the band to be accessed in lines.
     151             :  *
     152             :  * @param pData The buffer into which the data should be read, or from which
     153             :  * it should be written. This buffer must contain at least nBufXSize *
     154             :  * nBufYSize words of type eBufType. It is organized in left to right,
     155             :  * top to bottom pixel order. Spacing is controlled by the nPixelSpace,
     156             :  * and nLineSpace parameters.
     157             :  *
     158             :  * @param nBufXSize the width of the buffer image into which the desired region is
     159             :  * to be read, or from which it is to be written.
     160             :  *
     161             :  * @param nBufYSize the height of the buffer image into which the desired region is
     162             :  * to be read, or from which it is to be written.
     163             :  *
     164             :  * @param eBufType the type of the pixel values in the pData data buffer. The
     165             :  * pixel values will automatically be translated to/from the GDALRasterBand
     166             :  * data type as needed.
     167             :  *
     168             :  * @param nPixelSpace The byte offset from the start of one pixel value in
     169             :  * pData to the start of the next pixel value within a scanline. If defaulted
     170             :  * (0) the size of the datatype eBufType is used.
     171             :  *
     172             :  * @param nLineSpace The byte offset from the start of one scanline in
     173             :  * pData to the start of the next. If defaulted (0) the size of the datatype
     174             :  * eBufType * nBufXSize is used.
     175             :  *
     176             :  * @param psExtraArg (new in GDAL 2.0) pointer to a GDALRasterIOExtraArg structure with additional
     177             :  * arguments to specify resampling and progress callback, or NULL for default
     178             :  * behaviour. The GDAL_RASTERIO_RESAMPLING configuration option can also be defined
     179             :  * to override the default resampling to one of BILINEAR, CUBIC, CUBICSPLINE,
     180             :  * LANCZOS, AVERAGE or MODE.
     181             :  *
     182             :  * @return CE_Failure if the access fails, otherwise CE_None.
     183             :  */
     184             :

     438             : /************************************************************************/
     439             : /*                             ReadBlock()                              */
     440             : /************************************************************************/
     441             : 
     442             : /**
     443             :  * \brief Read a block of image data efficiently.
     444             :  *
     445             :  * This method accesses a "natural" block from the raster band without
     446             :  * resampling, or data type conversion.  For a more generalized, but
     447             :  * potentially less efficient access use RasterIO().
     448             :  *
     449             :  * This method is the same as the C GDALReadBlock() function.
     450             :  *
     451             :  * See the GetLockedBlockRef() method for a way of accessing internally cached
     452             :  * block oriented data without an extra copy into an application buffer.
     453             :  *
     454             :  * The following code would efficiently compute a histogram of eight bit
     455             :  * raster data.  Note that the final block may be partial ... data beyond
     456             :  * the edge of the underlying raster band in these edge blocks is of an
     457             :  * undermined value.
     458             :  *
     459             : \code{.cpp}
     460             :  CPLErr GetHistogram( GDALRasterBand *poBand, GUIntBig *panHistogram )
     461             : 
     462             :  {
     463             :      memset( panHistogram, 0, sizeof(GUIntBig) * 256 );
     464             : 
     465             :      CPLAssert( poBand->GetRasterDataType() == GDT_Byte );
     466             : 
     467             :      int nXBlockSize, nYBlockSize;
     468             : 
     469             :      poBand->GetBlockSize( &nXBlockSize, &nYBlockSize );
     470             :      int nXBlocks = (poBand->GetXSize() + nXBlockSize - 1) / nXBlockSize;
     471             :      int nYBlocks = (poBand->GetYSize() + nYBlockSize - 1) / nYBlockSize;
     472             : 
     473             :      GByte *pabyData = (GByte *) CPLMalloc(nXBlockSize * nYBlockSize);
     474             : 
     475             :      for( int iYBlock = 0; iYBlock < nYBlocks; iYBlock++ )
     476             :      {
     477             :          for( int iXBlock = 0; iXBlock < nXBlocks; iXBlock++ )
     478             :          {
     479             :              int        nXValid, nYValid;
     480             : 
     481             :              poBand->ReadBlock( iXBlock, iYBlock, pabyData );
     482             : 
     483             :              // Compute the portion of the block that is valid
     484             :              // for partial edge blocks.

     848             : 
     849             : /**
     850             :  * \brief Fetch the "natural" block size of this band.
     851             :  *
     852             :  * GDAL contains a concept of the natural block size of rasters so that
     853             :  * applications can organized data access efficiently for some file formats.
     854             :  * The natural block size is the block size that is most efficient for
     855             :  * accessing the format.  For many formats this is simple a whole scanline
     856             :  * in which case *pnXSize is set to GetXSize(), and *pnYSize is set to 1.
     857             :  *
     858             :  * However, for tiled images this will typically be the tile size.
     859             :  *
     860             :  * Note that the X and Y block sizes don't have to divide the image size
     861             :  * evenly, meaning that right and bottom edge blocks may be incomplete.
     862             :  * See ReadBlock() for an example of code dealing with these issues.
     863             :  *
     864             :  * This method is the same as the C function GDALGetBlockSize().
     865             :  *
     866             :  * @param pnXSize integer to put the X block size into or NULL.
     867             :  *
     868             :  * @param pnYSize integer to put the Y block size into or NULL.
     869             :  */

    1205             : 
    1206             : /**
    1207             :  * \brief Fetch a pointer to an internally cached raster block.
    1208             :  *
    1209             :  * This method will returned the requested block (locked) if it is already
    1210             :  * in the block cache for the layer.  If not, the block will be read from
    1211             :  * the driver, and placed in the layer block cached, then returned.  If an
    1212             :  * error occurs reading the block from the driver, a NULL value will be
    1213             :  * returned.
    1214             :  *
    1215             :  * If a non-NULL value is returned, then a lock for the block will have been
    1216             :  * acquired on behalf of the caller.  It is absolutely imperative that the
    1217             :  * caller release this lock (with GDALRasterBlock::DropLock()) or else
    1218             :  * severe problems may result.
    1219             :  *
    1220             :  * Note that calling GetLockedBlockRef() on a previously uncached band will
    1221             :  * enable caching.
    1222             :  *
    1223             :  * @param nXBlockOff the horizontal block offset, with zero indicating
    1224             :  * the left most block, 1 the next block and so forth.

    1227             :  * the top most block, 1 the next block and so forth.
    1228             :  *

    1230             :  * but not actually read from the source.  This is useful when it will just
    1231             :  * be completely set and written back.

    1233             :  * @return pointer to the block object, or NULL on failure.
    1234             :  */

    2400             :  * \brief Fetch the raster value offset.
    2401             :  *
    2402             :  * This value (in combination with the GetScale() value) can be used to
    2403             :  * transform raw pixel values into the units returned by GetUnitType().
    2404             :  * For example this might be used to store elevations in GUInt16 bands
    2405             :  * with a precision of 0.1, and starting from -100.
    2406             :  *
    2407             :  * Units value = (raw value * scale) + offset
    2408             :  *

    2410             :  * and is not done by methods such as RasterIO() or ReadBlock().
    2411             :  *
    2412             :  * For file formats that don't know this intrinsically a value of zero
    2413             :  * is returned.
    2414             :  *
    2415             :  * This method is the same as the C function GDALGetRasterOffset().
    2416             :  *
    2417             :  * @param pbSuccess pointer to a boolean to use to indicate if the
    2418             :  * returned value is meaningful or not.  May be NULL (default).
    2419             :  *

    2885             : 
    2886             : /**
    2887             :  * \brief Compute raster histogram.
    2888             :  *
    2889             :  * Note that the bucket size is (dfMax-dfMin) / nBuckets.
    2890             :  *
    2891             :  * For example to compute a simple 256 entry histogram of eight bit data,
    2892             :  * the following would be suitable.  The unusual bounds are to ensure that
    2893             :  * bucket boundaries don't fall right on integer values causing possible errors
    2894             :  * due to rounding after scaling.
    2895             : \code{.cpp}
    2896             :     GUIntBig anHistogram[256];
    2897             : 
    2898             :     poBand->GetHistogram( -0.5, 255.5, 256, anHistogram, FALSE, FALSE,
    2899             :                           GDALDummyProgress, nullptr );
    2900             : \endcode
    2901             :  *
    2902             :  * Note that setting bApproxOK will generally result in a subsampling of the
    2903             :  * file, and will utilize overviews if available.  It should generally
    2904             :  * produce a representative histogram for the data that is suitable for use
    2905             :  * in generating histogram based luts for instance.  Generally bApproxOK is
    2906             :  * much faster than an exactly computed histogram.
    2907             :  *
    2908             :  * This method is the same as the C functions GDALGetRasterHistogram() and
    2909             :  * GDALGetRasterHistogramEx().
    2910             :  *
    2911             :  * @param dfMin the lower bound of the histogram.
    2912             :  * @param dfMax the upper bound of the histogram.
    2913             :  * @param nBuckets the number of buckets in panHistogram.
    2914             :  * @param panHistogram array into which the histogram totals are placed.
    2915             :  * @param bIncludeOutOfRange if TRUE values below the histogram range will
    2916             :  * mapped into panHistogram[0], and values above will be mapped into
    2917             :  * panHistogram[nBuckets-1] otherwise out of range values are discarded.
    2918             :  * @param bApproxOK TRUE if an approximate, or incomplete histogram OK.
    2919             :  * @param pfnProgress function to report progress to completion.
    2920             :  * @param pProgressData application data to pass to pfnProgress.
    2921             :  *
    2922             :  * @return CE_None on success, or CE_Failure if something goes wrong.

    3637             : /**
    3638             :  * \fn GDALRasterBand::AdviseRead(int,int,int,int,int,int,GDALDataType,char**)
    3639             :  * \brief Advise driver of upcoming read requests.
    3640             :  *
    3641             :  * Some GDAL drivers operate more efficiently if they know in advance what
    3642             :  * set of upcoming read requests will be made.  The AdviseRead() method allows
    3643             :  * an application to notify the driver of the region of interest,
    3644             :  * and at what resolution the region will be read.
    3645             :  *
    3646             :  * Many drivers just ignore the AdviseRead() call, but it can dramatically
    3647             :  * accelerate access via some drivers.
    3648             :  *
    3649             :  * Depending on call paths, drivers might receive several calls to
    3650             :  * AdviseRead() with the same parameters.
    3651             :  *
    3652             :  * @param nXOff The pixel offset to the top left corner of the region
    3653             :  * of the band to be accessed.  This would be zero to start from the left side.
    3654             :  *
    3655             :  * @param nYOff The line offset to the top left corner of the region
    3656             :  * of the band to be accessed.  This would be zero to start from the top.
    3657             :  *
    3658             :  * @param nXSize The width of the region of the band to be accessed in pixels.
    3659             :  *
    3660             :  * @param nYSize The height of the region of the band to be accessed in lines.
    3661             :  *
    3662             :  * @param nBufXSize the width of the buffer image into which the desired region
    3663             :  * is to be read, or from which it is to be written.
    3664             :  *
    3665             :  * @param nBufYSize the height of the buffer image into which the desired
    3666             :  * region is to be read, or from which it is to be written.
    3667             :  *
    3668             :  * @param eBufType the type of the pixel values in the pData data buffer.  The
    3669             :  * pixel values will automatically be translated to/from the GDALRasterBand
    3670             :  * data type as needed.
    3671             :  *
    3672             :  * @param papszOptions a list of name=value strings with special control
    3673             :  * options.  Normally this is NULL.
    3674             :  *
    3675             :  * @return CE_Failure if the request is invalid and CE_None if it works or
    3676             :  * is ignored.
    3677             :  */
    3678             : 
    3679             : /**/
    3680             : /**/

    5904             : 
    5905             : /**
    5906             :  * \brief Return the mask band associated with the band.
    5907             :  *
    5908             :  * The GDALRasterBand class includes a default implementation of GetMaskBand() that
    5909             :  * returns one of four default implementations :
    5910             :  * <ul>
    5911             :  * <li>If a corresponding .msk file exists it will be used for the mask band.</li>
    5912             :  * <li>If the dataset has a NODATA_VALUES metadata item, an instance of the
    5913             :  *     new GDALNoDataValuesMaskBand class will be returned.
    5914             :  *     GetMaskFlags() will return GMF_NODATA | GMF_PER_DATASET. @since GDAL 1.6.0</li>
    5915             :  * <li>If the band has a nodata value set, an instance of the new
    5916             :  *     GDALNodataMaskRasterBand class will be returned.
    5917             :  *     GetMaskFlags() will return GMF_NODATA.</li>
    5918             :  * <li>If there is no nodata value, but the dataset has an alpha band that seems
    5919             :  *     to apply to this band (specific rules yet to be determined) and that is
    5920             :  *     of type GDT_Byte then that alpha band will be returned, and the flags
    5921             :  *     GMF_PER_DATASET and GMF_ALPHA will be returned in the flags.</li>
    5922             :  * <li>If neither of the above apply, an instance of the new GDALAllValidRasterBand
    5923             :  *     class will be returned that has 255 values for all pixels.
    5924             :  *     The null flags will return GMF_ALL_VALID.</li>
    5925             :  * </ul>
    5926             :  *
    5927             :  * Note that the GetMaskBand() should always return a GDALRasterBand mask, even
    5928             :  * if it is only an all 255 mask with the flags indicating GMF_ALL_VALID.
    5929             :  *
    5930             :  * For an external .msk file to be recognized by GDAL, it must be a valid GDAL
    5931             :  * dataset, with the same name as the main dataset and suffixed with .msk,
    5932             :  * with either one band (in the GMF_PER_DATASET case), or as many bands as the
    5933             :  * main dataset.
    5934             :  * It must have INTERNAL_MASK_FLAGS_xx metadata items set at the dataset
    5935             :  * level, where xx matches the band number of a band of the main dataset. The
    5936             :  * value of those items is a combination of the flags GMF_ALL_VALID,
    5937             :  * GMF_PER_DATASET, GMF_ALPHA and GMF_NODATA. If a metadata item is missing for
    5938             :  * a band, then the other rules explained above will be used to generate a
    5939             :  * on-the-fly mask band.
    5940             :  * \see CreateMaskBand() for the characteristics of .msk files created by GDAL.
    5941             :  *
    5942             :  * This method is the same as the C function GDALGetMaskBand().

    6157             : /************************************************************************/
    6158             : /*                            GetMaskFlags()                            */
    6159             : /************************************************************************/
    6160             : 
    6161             : /**
    6162             :  * \brief Return the status flags of the mask band associated with the band.
    6163             :  *
    6164             :  * The GetMaskFlags() method returns an bitwise OR-ed set of status flags with
    6165             :  * the following available definitions that may be extended in the future:
    6166             :  * <ul>
    6167             :  * <li>GMF_ALL_VALID(0x01): There are no invalid pixels, all mask values will be 255.
    6168             :  *     When used this will normally be the only flag set.</li>
    6169             :  * <li>GMF_PER_DATASET(0x02): The mask band is shared between all bands on the dataset.</li>
    6170             :  * <li>GMF_ALPHA(0x04): The mask band is actually an alpha band and may have values
    6171             :  *     other than 0 and 255.</li>
    6172             :  * <li>GMF_NODATA(0x08): Indicates the mask is actually being generated from nodata values.
    6173             :  *     (mutually exclusive of GMF_ALPHA)</li>
    6174             :  * </ul>
    6175             :  *
    6176             :  * The GDALRasterBand class includes a default implementation of GetMaskBand() that
    6177             :  * returns one of four default implementations :
    6178             :  * <ul>
    6179             :  * <li>If a corresponding .msk file exists it will be used for the mask band.</li>
    6180             :  * <li>If the dataset has a NODATA_VALUES metadata item, an instance of the
    6181             :  *     new GDALNoDataValuesMaskBand class will be returned.
    6182             :  *     GetMaskFlags() will return GMF_NODATA | GMF_PER_DATASET. @since GDAL 1.6.0</li>
    6183             :  * <li>If the band has a nodata value set, an instance of the new
    6184             :  *     GDALNodataMaskRasterBand class will be returned.
    6185             :  *     GetMaskFlags() will return GMF_NODATA.</li>
    6186             :  * <li>If there is no nodata value, but the dataset has an alpha band that seems
    6187             :  *     to apply to this band (specific rules yet to be determined) and that is
    6188             :  *     of type GDT_Byte then that alpha band will be returned, and the flags
    6189             :  *     GMF_PER_DATASET and GMF_ALPHA will be returned in the flags.</li>
    6190             :  * <li>If neither of the above apply, an instance of the new GDALAllValidRasterBand
    6191             :  *     class will be returned that has 255 values for all pixels.
    6192             :  *     The null flags will return GMF_ALL_VALID.</li>
    6193             :  * </ul>
    6194             :  *
    6195             :  * For an external .msk file to be recognized by GDAL, it must be a valid GDAL
    6196             :  * dataset, with the same name as the main dataset and suffixed with .msk,
    6197             :  * with either one band (in the GMF_PER_DATASET case), or as many bands as the
    6198             :  * main dataset.
    6199             :  * It must have INTERNAL_MASK_FLAGS_xx metadata items set at the dataset
    6200             :  * level, where xx matches the band number of a band of the main dataset. The
    6201             :  * value of those items is a combination of the flags GMF_ALL_VALID,
    6202             :  * GMF_PER_DATASET, GMF_ALPHA and GMF_NODATA. If a metadata item is missing for
    6203             :  * a band, then the other rules explained above will be used to generate a
    6204             :  * on-the-fly mask band.
    6205             :  * \see CreateMaskBand() for the characteristics of .msk files created by GDAL.
    6206             :  *
    6207             :  * This method is the same as the C function GDALGetMaskFlags().
    6208             :  *
    6209             :  * @since GDAL 1.5.0
    6210             :  *
    6211             :  * @return a valid mask band.
    6212             :  *
    6213             :  * @see http://trac.osgeo.org/gdal/wiki/rfc15_nodatabitmask
    6214             :  *
    6215             :  */
    6216       48060 : int GDALRasterBand::GetMaskFlags()
    6217             : 
    6218             : {

    6572             : /************************************************************************/
    6573             : /*                           GetVirtualMemAuto()                        */
    6574             : /************************************************************************/
    6575             : 
    6576             : /** \brief Create a CPLVirtualMem object from a GDAL raster band object.
    6577             :  *
    6578             :  * Only supported on Linux and Unix systems with mmap() for now.
    6579             :  *
    6580             :  * This method allows creating a virtual memory object for a GDALRasterBand,
    6581             :  * that exposes the whole image data as a virtual array.
    6582             :  *
    6583             :  * The default implementation relies on GDALRasterBandGetVirtualMem(), but specialized
    6584             :  * implementation, such as for raw files, may also directly use mechanisms of the
    6585             :  * operating system to create a view of the underlying file into virtual memory
    6586             :  * ( CPLVirtualMemFileMapNew() )
    6587             :  *
    6588             :  * At the time of writing, the GeoTIFF driver and "raw" drivers (EHdr, ...) offer
    6589             :  * a specialized implementation with direct file mapping, provided that some
    6590             :  * requirements are met :
    6591             :  *   - for all drivers, the dataset must be backed by a "real" file in the file
    6592             :  *     system, and the byte ordering of multi-byte datatypes (Int16, etc.)
    6593             :  *     must match the native ordering of the CPU.
    6594             :  *   - in addition, for the GeoTIFF driver, the GeoTIFF file must be uncompressed, scanline
    6595             :  *     oriented (i.e. not tiled). Strips must be organized in the file in sequential
    6596             :  *     order, and be equally spaced (which is generally the case). Only power-of-two
    6597             :  *     bit depths are supported (8 for GDT_Bye, 16 for GDT_Int16/GDT_UInt16,
    6598             :  *     32 for GDT_Float32 and 64 for GDT_Float64)
    6599             :  *
    6600             :  * The pointer returned remains valid until CPLVirtualMemFree() is called.
    6601             :  * CPLVirtualMemFree() must be called before the raster band object is destroyed.
    6602             :  *
    6603             :  * If p is such a pointer and base_type the type matching GDALGetRasterDataType(),
    6604             :  * the element of image coordinates (x, y) can be accessed with
    6605             :  * *(base_type*) ((GByte*)p + x * *pnPixelSpace + y * *pnLineSpace)
    6606             :  *
    6607             :  * This method is the same as the C GDALGetVirtualMemAuto() function.
    6608             :  *
    6609             :  * @param eRWFlag Either GF_Read to read the band, or GF_Write to
    6610             :  * read/write the band.
    6611             :  *
    6612             :  * @param pnPixelSpace Output parameter giving the byte offset from the start of one pixel value in
    6613             :  * the buffer to the start of the next pixel value within a scanline.
    6614             :  *
    6615             :  * @param pnLineSpace Output parameter giving the byte offset from the start of one scanline in
    6616             :  * the buffer to the start of the next.
    6617             :  *
    6618             :  * @param papszOptions NULL terminated list of options.
    6619             :  *                     If a specialized implementation exists, defining USE_DEFAULT_IMPLEMENTATION=YES
    6620             :  *                     will cause the default implementation to be used.
    6621             :  *                     On the contrary, starting with GDAL 2.2, defining USE_DEFAULT_IMPLEMENTATION=NO
    6622             :  *                     will prevent the default implementation from being used (thus only allowing
    6623             :  *                     efficient implementations to be used).
    6624             :  *                     When requiring or falling back to the default implementation, the following
    6625             :  *                     options are available : CACHE_SIZE (in bytes, defaults to 40 MB),
    6626             :  *                     PAGE_SIZE_HINT (in bytes),
    6627             :  *                     SINGLE_THREAD ("FALSE" / "TRUE", defaults to FALSE)
    6628             :  *
    6629             :  * @return a virtual memory object that must be unreferenced by CPLVirtualMemFree(),
    6630             :  *         or NULL in case of failure.
    6631             :  *
    6632             :  * @since GDAL 1.11
    6633             :  */
    6634             :

    6698             : /************************************************************************/
    6699             : /*                        GDALGetDataCoverageStatus()                   */
    6700             : /************************************************************************/
    6701             : 
    6702             : /**
    6703             :  * \brief Get the coverage status of a sub-window of the raster.
    6704             :  *
    6705             :  * Returns whether a sub-window of the raster contains only data, only empty
    6706             :  * blocks or a mix of both. This function can be used to determine quickly
    6707             :  * if it is worth issuing RasterIO / ReadBlock requests in datasets that may
    6708             :  * be sparse.
    6709             :  *
    6710             :  * Empty blocks are blocks that are generally not physically present in the
    6711             :  * file, and when read through GDAL, contain only pixels whose value is the
    6712             :  * nodata value when it is set, or whose value is 0 when the nodata value is
    6713             :  * not set.
    6714             :  *
    6715             :  * The query is done in an efficient way without reading the actual pixel
    6716             :  * values. If not possible, or not implemented at all by the driver,
    6717             :  * GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_UNIMPLEMENTED | GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_DATA will
    6718             :  * be returned.
    6719             :  *
    6720             :  * The values that can be returned by the function are the following,
    6721             :  * potentially combined with the binary or operator :
    6722             :  * <ul>
    6723             :  * <li>GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_UNIMPLEMENTED : the driver does not implement
    6724             :  * GetDataCoverageStatus(). This flag should be returned together with
    6725             :  * GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_DATA.</li>
    6726             :  * <li>GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_DATA: There is (potentially) data in the queried
    6727             :  * window.</li>
    6728             :  * <li>GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_EMPTY: There is nodata in the queried window.
    6729             :  * This is typically identified by the concept of missing block in formats that
    6730             :  * supports it.
    6731             :  * </li>
    6732             :  * </ul>
    6733             :  *
    6734             :  * Note that GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_DATA might have false positives and
    6735             :  * should be interpreted more as hint of potential presence of data. For example
    6736             :  * if a GeoTIFF file is created with blocks filled with zeroes (or set to the
    6737             :  * nodata value), instead of using the missing block mechanism,
    6738             :  * GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_DATA will be returned. On the contrary,
    6739             :  * GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_EMPTY should have no false positives.
    6740             :  *
    6741             :  * The nMaskFlagStop should be generally set to 0. It can be set to a
    6742             :  * binary-or'ed mask of the above mentioned values to enable a quick exiting of
    6743             :  * the function as soon as the computed mask matches the nMaskFlagStop. For
    6744             :  * example, you can issue a request on the whole raster with nMaskFlagStop =
    6745             :  * GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_EMPTY. As soon as one missing block is encountered,
    6746             :  * the function will exit, so that you can potentially refine the requested area
    6747             :  * to find which particular region(s) have missing blocks.
    6748             :  *
    6749             :  * @see GDALRasterBand::GetDataCoverageStatus()
    6750             :  *
    6751             :  * @param hBand raster band
    6752             :  *
    6753             :  * @param nXOff The pixel offset to the top left corner of the region
    6754             :  * of the band to be queried. This would be zero to start from the left side.
    6755             :  *
    6756             :  * @param nYOff The line offset to the top left corner of the region
    6757             :  * of the band to be queried. This would be zero to start from the top.
    6758             :  *
    6759             :  * @param nXSize The width of the region of the band to be queried in pixels.
    6760             :  *
    6761             :  * @param nYSize The height of the region of the band to be queried in lines.
    6762             :  *
    6763             :  * @param nMaskFlagStop 0, or a binary-or'ed mask of possible values
    6764             :  * GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_UNIMPLEMENTED,
    6765             :  * GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_DATA and GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_EMPTY. As soon
    6766             :  * as the computation of the coverage matches the mask, the computation will be
    6767             :  * stopped. *pdfDataPct will not be valid in that case.
    6768             :  *
    6769             :  * @param pdfDataPct Optional output parameter whose pointed value will be set
    6770             :  * to the (approximate) percentage in [0,100] of pixels in the queried
    6771             :  * sub-window that have valid values. The implementation might not always be
    6772             :  * able to compute it, in which case it will be set to a negative value.
    6773             :  *
    6774             :  * @return a binary-or'ed combination of possible values
    6775             :  * GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_UNIMPLEMENTED,
    6776             :  * GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_DATA and GDAL_DATA_COVERAGE_STATUS_EMPTY
    6777             :  *
    6778             :  * @note Added in GDAL 2.2
    6779             :  */
    6780             : 
    6781           8 : int CPL_STDCALL GDALGetDataCoverageStatus( GDALRasterBandH hBand,

    6785             :                                int nMaskFlagStop,
    6786             :                                double* pdfDataPct)
    6787             : {
